    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer1634804746194914456"><< Songez-vous au suicide? Pas de panique, vous n'êtes pas seul. Nous sommes plusieurs à partager les mêmes idées, et même un début d'expérience.   <span id="freeText1634804746194914456" style="display:none">&lt;&lt; Songez-vous au suicide? Pas de panique, vous n'êtes pas seul. Nous sommes plusieurs à partager les mêmes idées, et même un début d'expérience. Ecrivez-nous en exposant brièvement votre situation, peut-être pourrons-nous vous aider. Joignez vos nom et adresse, nous vous contacterons. Toutes les informations recueillies seront considérées comme strictement confidentielles et ne seront communiquées à aucun tiers. Pas sérieux s'abstenir. Veuillez adresser vos réponses Poste restante, Bureau central de Helsinki, nom de code " Essayons ensemble ". &gt;&gt;<br />Deux suicidaires se retrouvent fortuitement dans une vieille grange où ils souhaitaient partir tranquilles. Entravés dans leurs funestes projets, ils se mettent en tête de rassembler d'autres désespérés pour monter une association. Commence alors, à bord d'un car de tourisme flambant neuf, un périple loufoque mené à un train d'enfer, des falaises de l'océan Arctique jusqu'au cap Saint-Vincent au Portugal pour un saut de l'ange final. Un récit désopilant doublé d'une réflexion mordante sur le suicide.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1634804746194914456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3194757448" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3194757448" />
    <a title="Ivana Books Are Magic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56173179-ivana-books-are-magic"><img alt="Ivana Books Are Magic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578249636p2/56173179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3194757448?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana Books Are Magic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana Books Are Magic" href="/user/show/56173179-ivana-books-are-magic">Ivana Books Are Magic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3194757448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9320831139934287624">What a wonderful and original novel! Written by a Finnish author I wasn't familiar with prior to reading this book, this novel absolutely charmed me. Oddly funny in a dark way, this is a story of a group of suicidal people who decide to commit suicide together. They all have their reasons for wanting to end their life. Some of them have quite serious reasons and yet there is humour in this book (dark humour that is). <br/><br/>They embark on a long journey, slowly postponing the date of their suicide. At </span>
  <span id="freeText9320831139934287624" style="display:none">What a wonderful and original novel! Written by a Finnish author I wasn't familiar with prior to reading this book, this novel absolutely charmed me. Oddly funny in a dark way, this is a story of a group of suicidal people who decide to commit suicide together. They all have their reasons for wanting to end their life. Some of them have quite serious reasons and yet there is humour in this book (dark humour that is). <br /><br />They embark on a long journey, slowly postponing the date of their suicide. At one point they get themselves a bus, an eventual means of their planned suicide (they want to drive themselves off the cliff) but first they decide to drive around the country. Friendships and love attachments are formed, as these lonely individuals find understanding and support in one another. However, will this excursion be enough to make them crave life or will they eventually commit suicide together?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9320831139934287624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6020812862792721886">Definitely one of my favourite books, just brillant.<br/>The author have a gift to treat the worst subjects possible like madness, murder, cheating, loneliness and here suicidal tendencies with a sense of humor never seen before. No matter how you feel, you can read him and find yourself smiling over tragic issues and realizing that after all even the thin</span>
  <span id="freeText6020812862792721886" style="display:none">Definitely one of my favourite books, just brillant.<br />The author have a gift to treat the worst subjects possible like madness, murder, cheating, loneliness and here suicidal tendencies with a sense of humor never seen before. But a humor that is for once not without respect for the subjects he treats and the people dealing with it, that's the force of Paasilinna for me. No matter how you feel, you can read him and find yourself smiling over tragic issues and realizing that after all even the things that seems impossible to go over can be handle. Some quotes like "you can joke about death but not about life" are really representative of the book's spirit for me and are more than just some lines but really life mottos.<br />I've been taking this book around since I'm 13 and 10 years later it's still a all-time classic for me. I read enough times not to be able to count them anymore and I think it helped me a lot too in a strange way. It's just essential, if you haven't read it know that you NEED to.<br />If there is one book I would hand up to my friends (and I already bought i don't know how many copies of it as presents - weird ones, I give it to you but worth it - )it's this one and Lost Souls from Poppy Z Brite. <br /><br />DON'T THINK, JUST READ IT!</span>

<div id="review_2735485482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2735485482" />
    <a title="Nico Genes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65664660-nico-genes"><img alt="Nico Genes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526913723p2/65664660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2735485482?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nico Genes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nico Genes" href="/user/show/65664660-nico-genes">Nico Genes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/6163991-a-charming-mass-suicide">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65664660-nico-genes?shelf=sarcasm">sarcasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65664660-nico-genes?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735485482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11786235913173771362"><b>Ironic, humorous and ingenious read.</b><br/><br/>Two Finns meet by chance in an old barn, both intending to commit suicide, each in his own way. Their initial plan fails to materialize. This situation though makes them talk for the following days about their lives and their reasons to end it. They also realize little pleasures they had never noticed. Still, they decide to put an ad in a newspaper for all those who think alike. Surprisingly many people had answered their ad so they had to adjust their plans. </span>
  <span id="freeText11786235913173771362" style="display:none"><b>Ironic, humorous and ingenious read.</b><br /><br />Two Finns meet by chance in an old barn, both intending to commit suicide, each in his own way. Their initial plan fails to materialize. This situation though makes them talk for the following days about their lives and their reasons to end it. They also realize little pleasures they had never noticed. Still, they decide to put an ad in a newspaper for all those who think alike. Surprisingly many people had answered their ad so they had to adjust their plans. They end up organizing a seminar after which some of them decide to commit group suicide, by crashing with a bus into a ravine.<br /><br />Despite what we may think from the title and from the first pages of this book, this is not only about suicidal plans but actually, a hymn to life - which resists despite everything, wants only to find its own way outside conformism. Life is hard but when we meet people that feel the same we may reconsider certain thoughts, decisions. This book is also an invitation to friendship, to sharing, but not the superficial one, the one that really manages to enrich, to give a new perspective, new hopes, desire to live. <br /><br /><i>Type of reader:</i> Fans of contemporary fiction with a touch of sarcasm.<br /><br />More book reviews on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.nicojgenes.com/book-reviews">https://www.nicojgenes.com/book-reviews</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11786235913173771362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13237224944750056437" style="display:none">“Contemplating suicide? Don’t worry, you are not alone!”<br /><br />Thus begins the attempt of two men, who feel they have nothing to live for, to found a group for other suicidal people so that they don’t have to die alone.<br /><br />After attracting more members than they had believed possible, the group sits down to discuss how to go about the business of dying. Their suicide attempts become ever more desperate as they travel across Europe, trying to find the perfect place to die. At almost every turn the group is foiled… by itself.<br /><br />With each attempt, the Spectacular Group Suicide members explore their own and each others’ reasons for wanting to end their lives. For the first time in months (and years, in some cases), they start to talk about what they are going through.<br /><br />Paasilinna takes on one of the most difficult subjects to come to terms with. Using bleak humour, shocking (but sadly true) statistics and a surprising level of sensitivity, he tackles Finland’s greatest killer<br /><br /><br /><a href="http://www.wildnightin.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">full review on my website</a></span>

<div id="review_3092423911" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3092423911" />
    <a title="Moon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89157725-moon"><img alt="Moon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592407519p2/89157725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3092423911?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Moon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Moon" href="/user/show/89157725-moon">Moon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 8611169492" href="/book/show/8137624-o-arljivi-skupinski-samomor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3092423911&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3092423911" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3536715682984326887">Maybe I'm not getting the finnish humor. Which is not entirely implausible. But come on.<br/><br/>I get dark humor, I'm not an idiot. I know some people need to see the funny in the sadness of life but fucking come on. And again, maybe I've been too influenced by the 'PC culture' and seen one too many American comedies that have ruined my sense of humor but I didn't find this book amusing.<br/><br/>I found it infuriating. Are you making a group to help people or to assist them with suicide? Why do all the deaths th</span>
  <span id="freeText3536715682984326887" style="display:none">Maybe I'm not getting the finnish humor. Which is not entirely implausible. But come on.<br /><br />I get dark humor, I'm not an idiot. I know some people need to see the funny in the sadness of life but fucking come on. And again, maybe I've been too influenced by the 'PC culture' and seen one too many American comedies that have ruined my sense of humor but I didn't find this book amusing.<br /><br />I found it infuriating. Are you making a group to help people or to assist them with suicide? Why do all the deaths that do happen feel accidental? Did the author not feel, that making the living suicidal characters show up at the funeral of a 'successful' suicide victim a bit of a slap in the face of the victim's close ones?<br /><br />*here is where I complain about using the theme of suicide as a joke so if you're not into that just skip*<br />Where is the joke in making fun of something people actually go through and don't do just because they got bored of living? The juxtaposition between the characters that just had a bad episode in their lives and the woman whose kids apparently didn't care about her and the husband who degraded and physically abused her was fucking wild.<br /><br />I get that this book came out in 1990 but fuck me, domestic abuse wasn't funny 30 years ago and it isn't funny now.<br /><br />The sad part about this is that my highschool professor recommended this book in class and I highly respected his opinion. Now I'm super confused as to what he found entertaining about this.<br /><br />A group of people determined to commit mass suicide fuck around Europe searching for the perfect spot to do it, until they realise that none of them have any problems that a good break from their hum-drum lives can't fix. But some members still die and whoopsie! Send some flowers, attend the funeral and onward we go! <br /><br />I won't go into how damaging it is to depict characters as suicidal but make their problems seem trivial, so as to then go "and all they needed was some time away from their boring lives, isn't that funny". Right.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3536715682984326887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1941294083?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teri" href="/user/show/7050266-teri">Teri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789510165133" href="/book/show/656878.Hurmaava_joukkoitsemurha">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7050266-teri?shelf=buy-my-own-copy-for-a-reread">buy-my-own-copy-for-a-reread</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1941294083" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10017372252605861029">Norwegian audiobook.<br/>Title translation: The Charming Mass Suicide<br/><br/>This book was hilarious and absolutely charming. It was given to me by a friend who told me it was a particular type of humor that many people didn't get, but she thought I could appreciate it. When I started reading it I thought 'No way, this would be hilarious to everyone!' I then proceeded to share some funny excerpts with people and received reactions ranging from blank stares to straight out shaming me for my callousness. I the</span>
  <span id="freeText10017372252605861029" style="display:none">Norwegian audiobook.<br />Title translation: The Charming Mass Suicide<br /><br />This book was hilarious and absolutely charming. It was given to me by a friend who told me it was a particular type of humor that many people didn't get, but she thought I could appreciate it. When I started reading it I thought 'No way, this would be hilarious to everyone!' I then proceeded to share some funny excerpts with people and received reactions ranging from blank stares to straight out shaming me for my callousness. I then realized that maybe she was right. This book is like an inside joke; you have to have been there to get it. This book takes a morbid topic and gets you laughing because "you can joke about death, but not about life." (&lt;- In the book; I for one like to laugh at life too)<br /><br />It has a bit of a predictable ending, but it is an adorable adventure to get there. The book also introduces many of the different members of the suicide convention which gives you a nice view of the dramatic differences in the stories that brought them to the same place. I really liked this a lot, but my main reason for appreciating it was that I had recently read a book written by a psychologist who claimed that suicide is almost always spurred by a romantic break up. So I appreciated the emphasis of the different stories as it seemed like an acceptance and validation of experiences rather than the typical (though probably not intentional) response of downplaying people's experiences when they feel suicidal. <br /><br />This book is a bit heavy to read for a non Finnish person as the names of people and places are a bit unfamiliar and difficult to follow. I would actually like to get a hard copy because I think having the words typed out will make it easier to follow. On the audiobook I did get a little bit lost sometimes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10017372252605861029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6939403314263752421">Embarrassing confession of the day: until now, I had never read a novel by a Finnish author. Which might not seem that scandalous for most, given Finland's relatively tiny population and the fact that it is a crazy language which does not lend itself well to translation, and I do not speak Finnish. I would wager to say that most people outside of Finland haven't read any Finnish lit, aside from the Muumin stories. So why does it feel embarrassing to me? Because I am a Finn. Albeit a non-Finnish </span>
  <span id="freeText6939403314263752421" style="display:none">Embarrassing confession of the day: until now, I had never read a novel by a Finnish author. Which might not seem that scandalous for most, given Finland's relatively tiny population and the fact that it is a crazy language which does not lend itself well to translation, and I do not speak Finnish. I would wager to say that most people outside of Finland haven't read any Finnish lit, aside from the Muumin stories. So why does it feel embarrassing to me? Because I am a Finn. Albeit a non-Finnish speaking Finn, but a Finn nonetheless. And when the fact of my citizenship came to a Swede's attention at a recent party, he asked me what Finnish authors I like, and the silence that followed promptly led to my doing an online search and deciding to catch up on my cultural heritage. And so I came across Arto Paasilinna, an much-beloved author whose works have at least been translated into German, and so I picked this book to start with and am glad I did. In some ways it was exactly what I expected from Finnish lit: incredibly dark and incredibly funny. And yet surprisingly, it was also much more optimistic and cutesy than expected, which surprised my German self. <br />All in all, if you can get your hands on a translation of this, I highly recommend it! </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10104798511133361997">🇬🇧<br/>It's a very funny novel, even though the theme is suicide. The adventures of the Finnish Anonymous Deadee are told with an irony (and self-irony about Finn's characteristics and habits) that makes us smile throughout the book. But it also makes us think: the problems that afflict us sometimes seem to be crushing us, while changing our point of view would be enough to see them shrink. <br/>One of the jokes I liked most: "In two months he learned to speak Portuguese, which is not surprising since the</span>
  <span id="freeText10104798511133361997" style="display:none">🇬🇧<br />It's a very funny novel, even though the theme is suicide. The adventures of the Finnish Anonymous Deadee are told with an irony (and self-irony about Finn's characteristics and habits) that makes us smile throughout the book. But it also makes us think: the problems that afflict us sometimes seem to be crushing us, while changing our point of view would be enough to see them shrink. <br />One of the jokes I liked most: "In two months he learned to speak Portuguese, which is not surprising since the pronunciation of Portuguese and Sami has amazing affinities. Portuguese comes from late Latin, and sami comes from reindeer greed."<br />🇮🇹<br />Molto divertente nonostante il tema sia il suicidio. Le avventure dei morituri anonimi finlandesi sono raccontate con una ironia (e autoironia sulle caratteristiche e le abitudini dei finlandesi) che fa sorridere per tutto il libro. Ma fa anche riflettere su come i problemi che ci affliggono a volte sembrino schiacciarci mentre basterebbe cambiare punto di vista per vederli rimpicciolire.<br />Una delle battute che mi è piaciuta di più:<br />"In due mesi imparò a parlare portoghese, cosa che non stupisce dato che la pronuncia del portoghese e del sami presenta affinità sorprendenti. Il portoghese deriva dal tardo latino, e il sami dal bramito delle renne."</span>

<div id="review_46278863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46278863" />
    <a title="André" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/655975-andr"><img alt="André" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1196690794p2/655975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46278863?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="André" class="user" itemprop="url" name="André" href="/user/show/655975-andr">André</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Taschenbuch 9783404921683" href="/book/show/1030636.Der_wunderbare_Massenselbstmord">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to André by: </span>
      Stephanie Lego
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer46278863&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46278863" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17865310950306616805">Got this book for my 24th birthday from Stephi and as my second Paasilinna book, I found it about equally funny. It's really an amusing read and a well-written story. I especially like the hidden jokes and wit and how he writes about those suicidals in a very every-day stile. And the most I liked a little paragraph from the end of the book:<br/><br/><i>"Er lernte innerhalb von zwei Monaten Portugiesisch, was kein Wunder war, denn das Samische und das Portugiesische haben in der Aussprache überraschend viel g</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17865310950306616805" style="display:none">Got this book for my 24th birthday from Stephi and as my second Paasilinna book, I found it about equally funny. It's really an amusing read and a well-written story. I especially like the hidden jokes and wit and how he writes about those suicidals in a very every-day stile. And the most I liked a little paragraph from the end of the book:<br /><br /><i>"Er lernte innerhalb von zwei Monaten Portugiesisch, was kein Wunder war, denn das Samische und das Portugiesische haben in der Aussprache überraschend viel gemeinsam. Das Portugiesische hat sich aus dem Volkslatein entwickelt und das Samische aus dem Schnauben der Rentiere."</i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15887163765837835638">It's hard to rate this little gem any lower. Paasilinna's characteristic style of deadpanning absurdities and seemingly haphazard plot grows slightly boring after a while (having read two of his books now I feel like I've read them all), but the charm and wonderfully black humour of this book really won me over. The Finns' stoic matter-of-fact-ness in the face of death is absolutely hilarious, and the book succeeds in illuminating a lot of the best and the worst sides of Finnish life. And the ba</span>
  <span id="freeText15887163765837835638" style="display:none">It's hard to rate this little gem any lower. Paasilinna's characteristic style of deadpanning absurdities and seemingly haphazard plot grows slightly boring after a while (having read two of his books now I feel like I've read them all), but the charm and wonderfully black humour of this book really won me over. The Finns' stoic matter-of-fact-ness in the face of death is absolutely hilarious, and the book succeeds in illuminating a lot of the best and the worst sides of Finnish life. And the battle of Walsrode is one of the funniest scenes I've ever read.</span>

The only thing that bothered me at times was the repetitivity of certain jokes. Other than that, a wonderful and very lively little gem.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9788203211768" href="/book/show/12288044-kollektivt-selvmord">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17062131-anna?shelf=read-in-norwegian">read-in-norwegian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17062131-anna?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1657675879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer763983887394070449">This is a ... weird book. <i>Kollektivt selvmord</i>, or <i>A Charming Mass Suicide</i> as it is called in English, is a funny book about ... well ... suicide. It should be this funny, but it is. Arto Paasilinna manages to write about death in a funny and humorous way, and somehow it works. I have no idea why it works, but it does...</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2854261930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2854261930" />
    <a title="Patrizia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92163253-patrizia"><img alt="Patrizia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598439014p2/92163253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2854261930?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrizia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrizia" href="/user/show/92163253-patrizia">Patrizia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/27425655-piccoli-suicidi-tra-amici">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2854261930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer379995443713788656">I found this oddly uplifting and at times even funny. I found the irony used by Paasilinna quite poignant, it really did strike a chord with me. <br/>Death isn't that serious and neither is this book, I'd reccomend it to anyone who's comfortable with the discussion around suicide and even to those who aren't. Push yourself, what's the worst thing that could happen?</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iVh03xSObrFTgojgEDD2cHzh7t5ZshErb0eryL/RN4Au3ayrgxV3ac8wl2tzFn1objQKeu/RG0PsllnaOrSCpA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('svrBmgi7whFbuE1bbHt3LkgGbACXiWoqcJQLdxV4Xm4VfxnunyDbyccKUtAPXfw2WtOIpCHqYELzRfllkB3rSg==')})

fisica e di distinzioni sociali irriducibili, e dimostra che la storia di una famiglia, delle sue voci e delle sue traiettorie, è prima di tutto una storia del corpo e delle parole, in cui, a un certo <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6643441-la-vita-agra"><img alt="La vita agra" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1582655215l/6643441._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_6643441'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6643441-la-vita-agra?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">La vita agra<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/705963.Luciano_Bianciardi?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Luciano Bianciardi<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.06 avg rating &mdash; 780 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1962\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer12431651468999828988\">Questo romanzo, in larga parte autobiografico, si sarebbe potuto anche intitolare Missione impossibile e il perché lo comprenderete con le righe che seguono.\nLa vicenda prende origine dal disastro minerario di Ribolla nel 1954, in cui perirono 43 min<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12431651468999828988\" style=\"display:none\">Questo romanzo, in larga parte autobiografico, si sarebbe potuto anche intitolare Missione impossibile e il perché lo comprenderete con le righe che seguono.\nLa vicenda prende origine dal disastro minerario di Ribolla nel 1954, in cui perirono 43 minatori, per negligenza, ma soprattutto per calcoli di economia del padronato in cui il valore di una vita umana non rientrava minimamente.\nE’ così che il protagonista, nel desiderio di vendicare quegli innocenti, da buon anarchico vuole colpire il simbolo del potere che si annida in un palazzone di Milano, il torracchione, da far saltare con una giusta combinazione di aria e metano, proprio come era avvenuto per lo scoppio di grisù in miniera.\nIl proposito è ardito, la volontà è salda, ma la grande città è un mostro che piano piano ingloba, appiattisce, distrugge la vita e gli ideali.\nNemmeno il desiderio di coinvolgere i suoi cittadini schiavi in un moto di ribellione (bellissima la descrizione delle partenze degli operai alla sera dalla stazione Centrale di Milano) può trovare sbocco, perché in quei sudditi l’appiattimento si è trasformato in apatia e l’abitudine in rassegnazione, anzi è gente che crede di poter convivere con il mostro che li asservisce.\nE’ un’umanità impersonale, quasi i suoi componenti non avessero il volto, oppure questo è sistematicamente eguale fra le donne, una sorta di automi inaciditi e invecchiati prima del tempo, a cui al massimo è concessa la facoltà di far le scarpe agli altri, in una modesta carriera che assomiglia a uno scontro quotidiano. Solo una appare non inglobata, quella Anna di cui lui, già sposato con Mara rimasta al paese con il pargolo, si innamora perdutamente, per reazione e perché tanta è la differenza rispetto alle altre.\nIn concomitanza con la conoscenza di questa compagna di vita iniziano le pagine più autenticamente rivoluzionarie con una visione libera totalmente della vita sessuale, con un richiamo forte a un amore fisico secondo natura, scevro dall’ossessiva pubblicità che sembra dare e invece toglie tutto, in una satira della classe dirigente come prima non si era mai scritta.\nNell’attesa, sempre più disillusa, di arrivare a far saltare non solo il torracchione, ma il coperchio di potere che schiaccia la città, il protagonista, per mantenere sé, la sua compagna e la famiglia, è costretto a lavorare, a fare il traduttore di testi letterari che, nella realtà, come ebbe a dire Bianciardi, divenne poi la sua effettiva occupazione.\nE’ un lavoro duro, non valutato adeguatamente, in cui un intellettuale preparato, impegnato ore e ore, finisce presto in preda all’amarezza, a quella vita agra che dà il titolo al libro. Sono pagine intense, anche di profonda commozione e che riescono a dare la misura del disagio esistenziale. Al riguardo mi permetto di citare due righe, non di più, ma ampiamente sufficienti per comprendere l’agro della vita: “Non è un mestiere avventuroso; le sue gioie e i suoi dolori dall’esterno si vedono assai poco.”.\nE’ la disgregazione di un ideale, è una rassegnazione che si spegne dentro, con un finale profondamente triste: l’anarchico, in origine saldo, determinato, pieno di ardore, è stato avvinto dai tentacoli di quel sistema che lui voleva scardinare.\nLa sua è stata solo una missione impossibile.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12431651468999828988\" href=\"#\" <span id="freeTextContainer7875464988684742646"><b>Arto Tapio Paasilinna</b> was a Finnish writer, being a former journalist turned comic novelist. One of Finland's most successful novelists, he won a broad readership outside of Finland in a way few other Finnish authors have before. Translated into 27 languages, over seven million copies of his books have been sold worldwide, and he has been claimed as "instrumental in generating the current level of</span>
  <span id="freeText7875464988684742646" style="display:none"><b>Arto Tapio Paasilinna</b> was a Finnish writer, being a former journalist turned comic novelist. One of Finland's most successful novelists, he won a broad readership outside of Finland in a way few other Finnish authors have before. Translated into 27 languages, over seven million copies of his books have been sold worldwide, and he has been claimed as "instrumental in generating the current level of interest in books from Finland".</span>
